(src)="76345"> Willard Carroll " Will " Smith Jr.[2][3][4 ] ( born September 25 , 1968)[2 ] is an American actor , producer , rapper , and songwriter .
(src)="76346"> In April 2007 , Newsweek called him " the most powerful actor in Hollywood".[5 ] Smith has been nominated for five Golden Globe Awards and two Academy Awards , and has won four Grammy Awards .
(trg)="135"> Willard Carroll " Will " Smith Jr . [ 2 ] [ 3 ] [ 4 ] ( an haife shi a ranar 25 Satumba , 1968 ) [ 2 ]
(src)="76348"> Fatima Massaquoi-Fahnbulleh pronunciation : /ˈfætəmə , ˈfɑːtiːˌmɑː/ /ˈmæsækhwɑː/-(1904–1978) was a pioneering educator in Liberia .
(src)="76349"> After completing her education in the United States , she returned to Liberia in 1946 , where she contributed much to the cultural and social life of the country .
(trg)="136"> Fatima Massaquoi-Fahnbulleh pronunciation : / ˈfætəmə , ˈfɑːtiːˌmɑː / / ˈmæsækhwɑː / - ( 1904 – 1978 ) ta kasance a soma malama a Liberia .
(trg)="137"> Bayan kammala ta ilimi a Amirka , ta koma Liberia a shekarar 1946 , inda ta bayar da gudunmawar da yawa da al ' adu da kuma zamantakewa rai na kasar .
(src)="76350"> Born into a family of African royalty , Massaquoi grew up in the care of an aunt in Njagbacca , in the Garwula District of Grand Cape Mount County of southern Liberia .
(src)="76351"> After seven years , she returned to the northwestern part of the country in Montserrado County , where she began her schooling .
(src)="76352"> In 1922 she accompanied her father , a diplomat , to Hamburg , Germany , where she completed her studies in medicine at the University of Hamburg in 1937 .
(src)="76353"> She moved to the United States for further education , studying sociology and anthropology at Lane College , Fisk University and Boston University .
(src)="76354"> While in the US , she collaborated on a dictionary of the Vai language and wrote her autobiography , though a legal battle ensued over the rights to her story .
(src)="76355"> She won an injunction barring others from publishing and returned to Liberia in 1946 , immediately beginning collaboration to establish a university there , which would become the University of Liberia .
(trg)="138"> An haife ta a wani gidan iyalin sarautar Afirka , Massaquoi tayin girma a kula da wani inna a Njagbacca , a cikin Garwula  gundumar na Grand Cape Mount County na kudancin Laberiya .
(trg)="139"> Bayan shekara bakwai , sai ta koma zuwa ga  arewa yammacin ɓangare na kasar a cikin Montserrado County , inda ta fara ta makaranta .
(trg)="140"> A shakara alif 1922 ta raka mahaifinta , a jami ' in diflomasiyyar , zuwa  Hamburg , Jamus , inda ta kammala karatunta a magani , a Jami ' ar Hamburg shekara alif dari tara da talatin da bakwai ( 1937 ) .
(trg)="141"> Ta koma Amurka domin kara ilimi , don karanta ilimin halayyar zaman jama ' a da anthropology a  kwaleji Lane , Jami ' ar  Fisk  da Boston . 
(src)="76356"> Notes
(trg)="142"> Notes
(src)="76357"> References
(trg)="143"> References
(src)="76358"> Christianity[note 1 ] is an Abrahamic monotheistic[1 ] religion based on the life and teachings of Jesus Christ , who serves as the focal point for the religion .
(src)="76359"> It is the world 's largest religion,[2][3 ] with over 2.4  billion followers,[4][5][6 ] or 33 % of the global population , known as Christians.[note 2 ] Christians believe that Jesus is the Son of God and the savior of humanity whose coming as the Messiah ( the Christ ) was prophesied in the Old Testament.[7 ]
(trg)="144"> Christianity [ note 1 ] is an Abrahamic monotheistic [ 1 ] religion based on the life and teachings of Jesus Christ , who serves as the focal point for the religion .
(trg)="145"> It is the world ' s largest religion , [ 2 ] [ 3 ] with over 2.4  billion followers , [ 4 ] [ 5 ] [ 6 ] or 33 % of the global population , known as Christians . [ note 2 ] Christians believe that Jesus is the Son of God and the savior of humanity whose coming as the Messiah ( the Christ ) was prophesied in the Old Testament . [ 7 ]
(src)="76360"> 1 2 Christianity 's status as monotheistic is affirmed in , among other sources , the Catholic Encyclopedia ( article " Monotheism " ) ; William F. Albright , From the Stone Age to Christianity ; H. Richard Niebuhr ; About.com , Monotheistic Religion resources ; Kirsch , God Against the Gods ; Woodhead , An Introduction to Christianity ; The Columbia Electronic Encyclopedia Monotheism ; The New Dictionary of Cultural Literacy , monotheism ; New Dictionary of Theology , Paul , pp. 496–99 ; Meconi .

(src)="77029"> Google AdSense is a program run by Google that allows publishers in the Google Network of content sites to serve automatic text , image , video , or interactive media advertisements , that are targeted to site content and audience .
(src)="77030"> These advertisements are administered , sorted , and maintained by Google .
(src)="77031"> They can generate revenue on either a per-click or per-impression basis .
(src)="77032"> Google beta-tested a cost-per-action service , but discontinued it in October 2008 in favor of a DoubleClick offering ( also owned by Google).[2 ] In Q1 2014 , Google earned US $3.4 billion ( $13.6 billion annualized ) , or 22 % of total revenue , through Google AdSense.[3 ] AdSense is a participant in the AdChoices program , so AdSense ads typically include the triangle-shaped AdChoices icon.[4][5 ] This program also operates on HTTP cookies .
(src)="77033"> Over 14 million websites use AdSense.[6 ]
(trg)="804"> Google AdSense wata manhajar Google  ce da ke barin mawallafa a cikin  Cibiyar Google ta shafukan yanar gizo  su iya bada tallace-tallacen da aka rubutu , ko hotuna , ko bidiyo , ko tallan da za a iya hulɗa da su , duk ta hanya mai sauƙi kuma atomatik , waɗanda aka yi niyyar su je ga masu ziyarar shafin .
(trg)="805"> Kamfanin Goolge ne mai kula , mai tantance , da tafiyad da waɗannan tallan .
(trg)="806"> Suna iya samar da kuɗaɗan shiga ta hanyar danna tallan ( per-click )  ko  idan an nuna tallan ( per-impression ) .
(trg)="807"> A farkon kwatar shekara 2014 , Google ta sami bilyon $ 3.4 ( wato bilyon $ 13.6 a gabaɗayar shekarar ) , ko kashi 22 cikin ɗari a adadin kuɗaɗan shiga na Google ta hanyar Google AdSense . [ 3 ]  Sama da shafuka miliyan 14 ne ke amfani da AdSense . [ 6 ]

(src)="77198"> Layal Abboud ( Arabic : ليال عبود‎‎:pronounced  [ layāl ʿab'boud ] ; born 15 May 1982 ) is a Lebanese pop singer , folk music entertainer , sound-lyric poet , concert dancer , fit model , Muslim humanitarian and businesswoman.[1][2][3 ]
(trg)="958"> Layal Abboud ( Arabic : ليال عبود ‎ ‎ : pronounced  [ layāl ʿab ' boud ] ; haifaffen 15 Mayu 1982 ) wani dan kabilar Lebanon ne , mawaƙa na mawaƙa , mawaƙa mai raɗa-raye , raye-raye na raye-raye , dacewa da samfurin , Abokan Musulmi da kuma ' yan kasuwa .  [ 1 ] [ 2 ] [ 3 ]
(src)="77199"> Born to a musical family in the Southern Lebanese Tyrian village of Kniseh , Abboud is a former ISF officer and studied English literature at Lebanese University , translation at Beirut Arab University and musical expression at the American University of Science and Technology .
(src)="77200"> She appeared for the first time in the Studio El-Fan series debuts as a South Lebanese competitor from 2001–02 .
(src)="77201"> Abboud 's musical career flourished with the release of her first album Fi Shouq ( Arabic : في شوق‎‎ : on longing ) published in late 2007.[4 ] Sings in different Arabic dialects , famous for her presentation of lebanese folklore music and internal summer concerts.[5 ] Abboud is a singer member in the Syndicate of Professional Artists in Lebanon.[6 ]
(trg)="959"> An haife shi zuwa wani dangi na gargajiya a kudancin Labanon na kauyen Kniseh , Abboud tsohon jami ' in ISF ne kuma ya yi nazarin wallafe-wallafen Ingilishi a Jami ' ar Lebanon , fassara a Jami ' ar Larabawa Beirut da kuma jawabi a cikin Jami ' ar Kimiyya da fasahar Amurka .
(trg)="960"> Ta bayyana a karo na farko a cikin wasan kwaikwayon na El El-Fan a matsayin mai shiga gasar kudancin Labanon daga 2001-02 .
(trg)="961"> Abboud ya zama aikin kwaikwayon da aka yi da sakon ta farko na fi Shouq ( Larabci : في شوق : a nema ) da aka buga a ƙarshen 2007 . [ 4 ]  Rubuta a cikin harsunan Larabci daban-daban , shahararrun ta gabatar da labaran tarihin labanese da kuma wasan kwaikwayo na cikin rani na ciki . [ 5 ]  Abboud shi ne memba mai rairayi a cikin ƙungiyar masu sana ' a a Lebanon .. [ 6 ]

(src)="77208"> Balaraba Ramat Yakubu ( born 1959)[1 ] is a Nigerian author who writes in Hausa .
(src)="77209"> She is a leader in the genre of littattafan soyayya or " love literature " , and one of the very few Hausa-language writers whose work has been translated into English .
(src)="77210"> She has also worked as a screenwriter , producer , and director of Kannywood films .
(src)="77211"> Her stories have focused on issues such as forced marriages and women 's education .
(trg)="967"> Balaraba Ramat Yakubu  kwarariyar marubuciyar littafan Hausa ne da ake wa lakabi littattafan soyayya .
(trg)="968"> An haife ta a cikin birnin Kano  a a shekarar 1959 [ 1 ]  .
(trg)="969"> Tana daga kalilan marubuta da aka fassara littafinta zuwa harshen Inglishi .
(trg)="970"> Rubuce - rubucenta sun fi bada muhimmanci akan zamantakewar aure da kuma gwagwarmayar mata a rayuwar Hausawa .
(src)="77212"> Balaraba Ramat Yakubu is the younger sister of General Murtala Ramat Muhammed , who briefly served as the military ruler of Nigeria from 1975 until his assassination in 1976 .
(trg)="971"> Hajiya Balaraba kanwa ce ga tsohon shugaban kasar Nijeriya , marigayi Murtala Ramat Muhammed wanda aka yi wa juyin mulki a shekarar 1976 .
(src)="77213"> At the age of 13 , she was taken out of school and forced into an early marriage .
(src)="77214"> She has said that this is the reason she writes in Hausa rather than English.[2 ]
(trg)="972"> Tun tana karama ' yar shekara 13 aka cire ta daga makaranta aka yi mata aure , wannan ne ma dalilin da ya sa take rubuce - rubucent da harshen Hausa maimakon turanci . [ 2 ]
(src)="77215"> Balaraba Ramat started her career as the only woman member of the influential Kano-based writer 's club Raina Kama.[3 ] Her first novel , Budurwar Zuciya ( " Young at Heart " ) , was published in 1987 .
(src)="77216"> Her second and third novels , Alhaki Kwikwiyo Ne ...
(src)="77217"> ( " Sin Is a Puppy That Follows You Home " ) and Wa zai auri jahila ?
(src)="77218"> ( " Who Will Marry an Ignorant Woman ? " ) , followed in 1990 .
(src)="77219"> Alhaki Kwikwiyo Ne ... was adapted into a film by Abdulkareem Muhammed in 1998.[4 ]
(trg)="973"> Balaraba Ramat ta kasance mace tilo a cikin jagororin kungiyar marubuta mai suna Raina Kama . [ 3 ] Littafinta na farko shi ne Budurwar Zuciya wanda aka wallafa a shekarar 1987 .
(trg)="974"> Daga nan ta ci gaba da rubuce - rubuce har zuwa daga bisani ta shiga harkar rubutun fim tare da shiryawa .
(trg)="975"> A shekarar 1998 , Muhammed Abdulkareem ya mayar da littafinta , Alhaki Kwikwiyo Ne zuwa fim  1998 . [ 4 ]
(src)="77220"> An English translation of Alhaki Kuykuyo Ne ... , Sin Is a Puppy That Follows You Home , was published in 2012 by Blaft Publications , an Indian publishing house , to positive reviews.[5][6 ]
(trg)="976"> Har ila yau kuma , a shekarar 2012 , wani kamfanin dab ' i a kasar Indiya mai suna Blaft Publishers ya wallafa fassarar littafin Alhaki Kwikwiyo Ne zuwa Inglishi .
(trg)="977"> Littafin ya samu kyakkyawan yabo  [ 5 ] [ 6 ]
(src)="77221"> There is a literary prize named after her , the Balaraba Ramat Yakubu Literature Prize for Hausa Drama.[7 ]
(trg)="978"> An samar da wasu kyaututtuka ga matasan marubuta wanda aka rada wa kyautar sunan Balaraba Ramat Yakubu . [ 7 ]

(src)="77240"> Farooq Adamu Kperogi ( born 1973 ) , is a Nigerian academic , media scholar , public speaker and newspaper columnist .
(src)="77241"> As a former journalist , Kperogi had been a reporter and news editor at many Nigerian newspapers including the Daily Trust and the now defunct New Nigerian and Daily Triumph .
(trg)="984"> Farooq Adamu Kperogi ( an haifeshi 1973 ) tshohon dan jarida ne kuma malamin ilimin hanyoyin sadarwa na zamani a kasar Amurka .
(trg)="985"> Farooq yayi aikin jarida a gidaje jaridun Najeriya kamar  Daily Trust  da kuma tsohuwar jarida  New Nigerian  ta gwamnatin tarayya .
(src)="77242"> Kperogi was among the presidential speechwriters during Obasanjo 's administration and had taught journalism at Ahmadu Bello University and Kaduna Polytechnic .
(src)="77243"> He teaches journalism at Kennesaw State University in Georgia , United States.[2][3][4 ] He is also the author of Glocal English : The Changing Face and Forms of Nigerian English , published in 2015 , as the 96th volume in series of Berkeley Insights in Linguistics and Semiotic.[5][6 ]
(trg)="986"> [ 5 ] [ 6 ]
(src)="77244"> Kperogi was born in 1973 , in Okuta , Baruten local government area of Kwara State , Nigeria.[7 ] He attended Bayero University between 1993 and 1997 , where he received bachelor 's degree in mass communication .
(src)="77245"> He obtained a master 's degree in communication at the University of Louisiana at Lafayette and a Ph.D. from Georgia State University in the United States in 2011.[2 ]
(trg)="987"> [ 2 ]
(src)="77246"> After graduating from Bayero University , Kano , Kperogi started working as reporter with newspapers in Katsina and Kano before joining the Media Trust as correspondent for the now defunct Weekly Trust .
(src)="77247"> He also worked for the now defunct federal government-owned paper , the New Nigerian , in the early 2000s .
(src)="77248"> Kperogi began his academic career between 2000 and 2002 at Kaduna Polytechnic , where he taught journalism and mass communication .
(src)="77249"> He also taught at Ahmadu Bello University , Zaria for brief time in 2004.[3 ] Between 2002 and 2004 , Kperogi worked in President Olusequn Obasanjo 's administration as a presidential speechwriter and researcher .
(src)="77250"> Kperogi writes two columns , " Politics of Grammar " and " Notes from Atlanta " , for the Abuja-based Daily Trust weekend editions .
(trg)="988"> After graduating from Bayero University , Kano , Kperogi started working as reporter with newspapers in Katsina and Kano before joining the Media Trust as correspondent for the now defunct Weekly Trust .
(trg)="989"> He also worked for the now defunct federal government-owned paper , the New Nigerian , in the early 2000s .
(trg)="990"> Kperogi began his academic career between 2000 and 2002 at Kaduna Polytechnic , where he taught journalism and mass communication .
(trg)="991"> He also taught at Ahmadu Bello University , Zaria for brief time in 2004 . [ 3 ] Between 2002 and 2004 , Kperogi worked in President Olusequn Obasanjo ' s administration as a presidential speechwriter and researcher .
(trg)="992"> Kperogi writes two columns , " Politics of Grammar " and " Notes from Atlanta " , for the Abuja-based Daily Trust weekend editions .

(src)="77323"> A bank is a financial institution that accepts deposits from the public and creates credit.[1 ] Lending activities can be performed either directly or indirectly through capital markets .
(src)="77324"> Due to their importance in the financial stability of a country , banks are highly regulated in most countries .
(src)="77325"> Most nations have institutionalized a system known as fractional reserve banking under which banks hold liquid assets equal to only a portion of their current liabilities .
(src)="77326"> In addition to other regulations intended to ensure liquidity , banks are generally subject to minimum capital requirements based on an international set of capital standards , known as the Basel Accords .

(src)="77565"> 393 members of the pro Iranian Dawa Party ( a banned organisation ) were arrested as suspects of which 148 , including ten children , confessed to taking part in the plot .
(src)="77566"> It is believed more than 40 suspects died during interrogation or while in detention .
(src)="77567"> Those arrested who were found not guilty were either exiled if relatives of the convicted or released and returned to Dujail .
(src)="77568"> Only 96 of the 148 condemned were actually executed , two of the condemned were accidentally released while a third was mistakenly transferred to another prison and survived .
(src)="77569"> The 96 executed included four men mistakenly executed after having been found not guilty and ordered released .
(src)="77570"> The ten children were originally believed to have been among the 96 executed , but they had in fact been imprisoned near the city of Samawah . ↑ " Saddam Formally Charged " .

(trg)="1284"> 393 members of the pro Iranian Dawa Party ( a banned organisation ) were arrested as suspects of which 148 , including ten children , confessed to taking part in the plot .
(trg)="1285"> It is believed more than 40 suspects died during interrogation or while in detention .
(trg)="1286"> Those arrested who were found not guilty were either exiled if relatives of the convicted or released and returned to Dujail .
(trg)="1287"> Only 96 of the 148 condemned were actually executed , two of the condemned were accidentally released while a third was mistakenly transferred to another prison and survived .
(trg)="1288"> The 96 executed included four men mistakenly executed after having been found not guilty and ordered released .
(trg)="1289"> The ten children were originally believed to have been among the 96 executed , but they had in fact been imprisoned near the city of Samawah . ↑ " Saddam Formally Charged " .

(src)="77636"> Saddam Hussein Abd al-Majid al-Tikriti ( /hʊˈseɪn/ ; [ 5 ] Arabic : صدام حسين عبد المجيد التكريتي Ṣaddām Ḥusayn ʿAbd al-Maǧīd al-Tikrītī ; [ lower-alpha 1 ] 28 April 1937[lower-alpha 2 ]  – 30 December 2006 ) was President of Iraq from 16 July 1979 until 9 April 2003.[10 ] A leading member of the revolutionary Arab Socialist Ba'ath Party , and later , the Baghdad-based Ba'ath Party and its regional organization the Iraqi Ba'ath Party—which espoused Ba'athism , a mix of Arab nationalism and socialism—Saddam played a key role in the 1968 coup ( later referred to as the 17 July Revolution ) that brought the party to power in Iraq .
(trg)="1354"> Saddam Hussein Abd al-Majid al-Tikriti ( / hʊˈseɪn / ; [ 5 ]  Larabci : صدام حسين عبد المجيد التكريتي Ṣaddām Ḥusayn ʿAbd al-Maǧīd al-Tikrītī ; [ lower-alpha 1 ] 28 Afrilu1937 [ lower-alpha 2 ]  – 30 Disamba 2006 ) tsohon shugaban kasar Iraki ne daga 6 ga Yuli 1979 har 9 Afrilu 2003 . [ 10 ]

(src)="77638"> Nnenne Iwuji-Eme in 2018
(trg)="1356"> Nnenne Iwuji-Eme in 2018
(src)="77639"> NneNne Iwuji-Eme is a British diplomat .
(src)="77640"> In March 2018 , she was announced as the next High Commissioner of the United Kingdom to Mozambique : she will take up the appointment in July 2018.[1 ] She is the first black woman to be appointed a high commissioner by the United Kingdom.[2][3][4 ]
(trg)="1357"> NneNne Iwuji-Eme wani jami ' in diflomasiyyar Birtaniya.A watan Maris na shekara ta 2018 , an sanar da shi a matsayin Babban Kwamishinan Birtaniya na Birtaniya a Mozambique : za ta fara aikin sa a watan Yulin 2018 . [ 1 ]  Ita ce mace ta farko da za a ba da aikin babban kwamishinan kasar ta Ingila . [ 2 ] [ 3 ] [ 4 ]
(src)="77641"> Iwuji-Eme was born in Truro , Cornwall , England to parents who worked for the United Nations.[2 ] She was educated at a boarding school in Suffolk.[2 ] She studied economics at the University of Manchester.[2 ] She joined the Department for the Environment , Food and Rural Affairs ( DEFRA ) in 1999 as an economic advisor.[1 ] In 2002 , she moved to the Foreign and Commonwealth Office ( FCO ) as Head of Africa , Middle East and Transition Economies in its Economic Policy Department.[1 ]
(trg)="1358"> Iwuji-Eme An haife shi a Truro , Cornwall , Ingilaga iyaye da suka yi aiki don United Nations . [ 2 ]  Ta koyi a makarantar shiga  Suffolk . [ 2 ]  Tana nazarin ilimin tattalin arziki a Jami ' ar  Manchester . [ 2 ]  Ta shiga Ma ' aikatar muhalli , Abinci da Rural Affairs  ( DEFRA ) a 1999 a matsayin mai ba da shawara kan tattalin arziki . [ 1 ] A shekara ta 2002 , ta koma wurin Ofishin Harkokin Kasashen waje da Commonwealth ( FCO ) a matsayin Shugaban Afrika , Gabas ta Tsakiya da kuma Tattalin Arziƙin Tattalin Arziƙi a Yankin Harkokin Tattalin Arziƙi . (src)="77743"> Sunni Islam ( /ˈsuːni , ˈsʊni/ ) is the largest denomination of Islam .
(src)="77744"> Its name comes from the word Sunnah , referring to the exemplary behaviour of the Islamic prophet Muhammad.[1 ] The differences between Sunni and Shia Muslims arose from a disagreement over the choice of Muhammad 's successor and subsequently acquired broader political significance , as well as theological and juridical dimensions.[2 ]
(trg)="1442">'''Sunni Islam''' Shine bangare mafi girma daga cikin bangarorin addinin [[Musulunci]], Asalin sunan yazone daga kalmar ''SUNNAH'' (''wato koyi da yin dukkan abun da Annabi [[Muhammad]] (S.A.W) Ya aikata, ko Yayi umarni da a aikata ko kuma aka aikata shi a gabansa amma bai yi hani ba'').
(trg)="1443"> Bambanci tsakanin Akidun Sunnah da kuma na [ [ Shi ' a ] ] Ya samo asaline tun daga takaddama akan wanda ya cancanci ya jagoranci al ' umar Musulmai bayan Wafatin Annabi ( s.a.w ) wato [ ['''Khalifanci''']] .
(src)="77745"> According to Sunni traditions , Muhammad did not clearly designate a successor and the Muslim community acted according to his sunnah in electing his father-in-law Abu Bakr as the first caliph.[3][2 ] This contrasts with the Shi'a view , which holds that Muhammad announced at the event of Ghadir Khumm his son-in-law and cousin Ali ibn Abi Talib as his successor.[4][5][6][7][8 ] Unlike the first three caliphs , Ali was from the same clan as Muhammad , Banu Hashim , and Shia Muslims consider him legitimate , inter alia , by favour of his blood ties to Muhammad , too.[9][10 ] Political tensions between Sunnis and Shias continued with varying intensity throughout Islamic history and they have been exacerbated in recent times by ethnic conflicts and the rise of Wahhabism.[2 ]
(trg)="1444"> Amma a bangaren Mabiya [ [ Shi ' a ] ] kuwa sai sukace ai a ranar [ [ Ghadir Khumm ] ] Annabi ( s.a.w. ) ya sanar da cewa ba wanda zai gaje shi sai dan ' uwan sa kuma sirikin sa wato [ [ Aliyu Ibn Abi Talib ] ] , sun ce sabo da shi jinin sane kuma surukin sa wato mijin yarsa Sayyada [ [ Fatima Bint Nabiy ] ] .
(src)="77746"> As of 2009 , Sunni Muslims constituted 87–90 % of the world 's Muslim population.[11 ] Sunni Islam is the world 's largest religious denomination , followed by Catholicism.[12 ] Its adherents are referred to in Arabic as ahl as-sunnah wa l-jamāʻah ( " the people of the sunnah and the community " ) or ahl as-sunnah for short.[13][14 ] In English , its doctrines and practices are sometimes called Sunnism,[15 ] while adherents are known as Sunni Muslims , Sunnis , Sunnites and Ahlus Sunnah .
(src)="77747"> Sunni Islam is sometimes referred to as " orthodox Islam".[16][17][18 ] However , other scholars of Islam , such as John Burton believe that there 's no such thing as " orthodox Islam".[19 ]
(trg)="1445"> A shekarar 2009 Musulmai mabiya Sunnah sunkai 87 % zuwa 90 % .
(trg)="1446"> Haka zalika Mabiya Bangaren Sunnah sune bangare a [ [ Addini ] ] wanda sukafi ko wanne yawa a [ [ duniya ] ] bayan [ [ Katolika ] ] a Kiristanci .
(src)="77756"> Abū Bakr aṣ-Ṣiddīq ‘ Abdallāh bin Abī Quḥāfah ( Arabic : أبو بكر الصديق عبد الله بن أبي قحافة‎ ; c.
(src)="77757"> 573 CE  – 22 August 634 CE ) , popularly known as Abu Bakr ( أبو بكر),[1 ] was a senior companion ( Sahabi ) and—through his daughter Aisha[2]—the father-in-law of the Islamic prophet Muhammad .
(src)="77758"> Abu Bakr became the first openly declared Muslim outside Muhammad 's family.[3][4 ] Abu Bakr served as a trusted advisor to Muhammad .
(src)="77759"> During Muhammad 's lifetime , he was involved in several campaigns and treaties.[5 ]
(trg)="1447"> Cikakken sunan shi shine Abu Bakr as-siddik Abdallah bin Abi Quhafa Larabci أبوبكر الصديق عبدالله بن ابي قحافة Amma anfi sanin sa da Abubakar ( أبوبكر ) , Shine babban Sahabi kuma Surukin Manzon Allah ( s.a.w ) ta bangaren yarsa kuma matar Annabi ( s.a.w ) wato Ummuna A ' isha ( r.a ) .
(trg)="1448"> Abubakar ya kasance cikakken mai gaskiya wanda Annabi ( s.a.w ) ya gaskata shi har ma mutane na yi masa lakabi da Assadik wato Mai gaskiya
(src)="77766"> Umar ( /ˈuːmɑːr/ ) , also spelled Omar ( /ˈoʊmɑːr/ ; Arabic : عمر بن الخطاب‎ ʻUmar ibn al-Khaṭṭāb [ ˈʕomɑr- , ˈʕʊmɑr ɪbn alxɑtˤˈtˤɑːb ] , " Umar , Son of Al-Khattab " ; c.
(src)="77767"> 584 CE  – 3 November 644 CE ) , was one of the most powerful and influential Muslim caliphs in history.[6 ] He was a senior companion of the Prophet Muhammad .
(src)="77768"> He succeeded Abu Bakr ( 632–634 ) as the second caliph of the Rashidun Caliphate on 23 August 634 .
(src)="77769"> He was an expert Muslim jurist known for his pious and just nature , which earned him the epithet Al-Farooq ( " the one who distinguishes ( between right and wrong ) " ) .
(src)="77770"> He is sometimes referred to as Umar I by historians of Islam , since a later Umayyad caliph , Umar II , also bore that name .
(trg)="1449"> Umar , ko kuma Omar a larabci kuma عمربن ألحطب Umar Ibn Al ' Khattab da hausa Umaru dan Kaddabi Allah ya yarda da shi .
(trg)="1450"> Daya ne daga cikin manyan Sahabban Annabi Muhammad ( s.a.w ) , kuma shine na biyu cikin halifofin Musuluncu .
(trg)="1451"> Yana daya daga cikin Halifofinnan guda Hudu na Halifancin Annabta , sannan kuma yana daya daga cikin sahabbai goman da Annabi yayima bishara da au yan Aljanna ne tun suna Duniya .
(trg)="1452"> Umar ya kasan ce mai taka tsantsan tare da gudun duniya , kasancewar sa mutumin da yayi kaurin suna kwarai wajen rarrabewa tsakanin gaskiya da karya be yasa akayi masa lakabi da Al ' farook .
(src)="77773"> Umar was born in Mecca to the Banu Adi clan , which was responsible for arbitration among the tribes.[14 ] His father was Khattab ibn Nufayl and his mother was Hantama bint Hisham , from the tribe of Banu Makhzum .
(src)="77774"> In his youth he used to tend to his father 's camels in the plains near Mecca .
(src)="77775"> His merchant father was famed for his intelligence among his tribe.[15 ] Umar himself said : " My father , Al-Khattab was a ruthless man .
(src)="77776"> He used to make me work hard ; if I did n't work he used to beat me and he used to work me to exhaustion."[16 ]

(trg)="1458"> Ali [ lower-alpha 1 ] ( / ˈɑːli , ɑːˈliː / ; [ 7 ] Arabic : علي ‎ , translit .  ʿAlī , pronounced  [ ʕaliː ] ) ( 15 September 601 – 29 January 661 ) [ 2 ] [ 3 ] was the cousin and the son-in-law of Muhammad , the prophet of Islam .
(trg)="1459"> He ruled as the fourth caliph from 656 to 661 , but he is regarded as the rightful immediate successor to prophet Muhammad by the Shia Muslims .
(src)="77798"> Uthman ibn Affan ( Arabic : عثمان بن عفان‎ , translit .  ʿUthmān ibn ʿAffān ) , also known in English by the Turkish and Persian rendering , Osman ( 579 – 17 June 656 ) , was a companion of the Islamic prophet Muhammad and the third of the Rashidun , or " Rightly Guided Caliphs " .
(src)="77799"> Born into a prominent Meccan clan , Banu Umayya of the Quraysh tribe , he played a major role in early Islamic history , succeeding Umar ibn al-Khattab who died in office at the age of 59/60 years as caliph at the age of 64/65 years ( the second-oldest ruler ) .

(src)="77801"> Birni-N'Konni ( also Birnin-Konni or shortened to Konni/Bkonni ) is a town in Niger , lying on the border of Nigeria and the Kori River .
(src)="77802"> It is an important market town and transport hub and the 2001 census had a population of 44,663 .
(src)="77803"> The town is the historic centre of the small pre-colonial Hausa state of Konni .
(src)="77804"> The name is Hausa language for " Walled Town of Konni " , and many Hausa towns ( such as Zinder ) designate the old citadel neighbourhood the " Birni".[1 ]
(trg)="1463"> Birni-N ' Konni ( also Birnin-Konni or shortened to Konni / Bkonni ) is a town in Niger , lying on the border of Nigeria and the Kori River .
(trg)="1464"> It is an important market town and transport hub and the 2001 census had a population of 44,663 .
(trg)="1465"> The town is the historic centre of the small pre-colonial Hausa state of Konni .
(trg)="1466"> The name is Hausa language for " Walled Town of Konni " , and many Hausa towns ( such as Zinder ) designate the old citadel neighbourhood the " Birni " . [ 1 ]
(src)="77805"> Konni is known for its vernacular architecture including traditional granaries and is regarded as a centre for smuggling between Niger and Nigeria , in which some suburbs of the town are officially located .
(src)="77806"> Birni-N'Konni 's contemporary importance rests on the surrounding agricultural lands and its place on the N1 highway , the main east-west highway linking Niger 's capital Niamey and the nation 's main eastern cities of Maradi and Zinder .
(src)="77807"> It also sits astride one of several main routes between the Hausa populated territories of southern Niger and northern Nigeria , with the Nigerian transport and trade centre of Illela , Sokoto State just 18 km to the south .
(trg)="1467"> Konni is known for its vernacular architecture including traditional granaries and is regarded as a centre for smuggling between Niger and Nigeria , in which some suburbs of the town are officially located .

(trg)="1469"> It also sits astride one of several main routes between the Hausa populated territories of southern Niger and northern Nigeria , with the Nigerian transport and trade centre of Illela , Sokoto State just 18 km to the south .
(src)="77808"> The town was also the site of a major massacre on 8 May 1899 when the French Voulet–Chanoine Mission attacked the region .
